    <meta name="dc.description" content="Zinc oxide nanoparticles (ZnO-NPs) is one of the promising material as anode in sodium ion batteries (SIBs). However, due to the large mass and radius of Na-ions, designing electrode materials with high cycling efficiency remains a challenge. One of the attributions is from morphology of ZnO-NPs which can be altered during synthesis process. This study employs Mariposa Christia vespertilionis (MCV) leaves extract to produce ZnO-NP using green synthesis route. This method is safe and cost effective alternative to replace the common chemical methods. Phytochemical test of MCV contains phenols, flavonoids and alkaloids. The formation of ZnO-NPs after calcination at 700, 800 and 900&amp;nbsp;°C was confirmed via X-ray diffraction and Fourier-transforms infrared spectroscopy analysis. Scanning electron microscope images how irregular shape and agglomerated ZnO-NPs. The average particle sizes of ZnO-NPs range from 38 to 65&amp;nbsp;nm obtained from high-resolution transmission electron microscope. Nitrogen gas adsorption analysis revealed the pore size and pore volume decreased with the increasing calcination temperatures. The ZnO-NPs calcined at 700&amp;nbsp;°C exhibits the highest initial discharge capacity of 591 mAh g−1 at 0.1 C up to 100 cycles and better rate capability and could be further exploited as anode materials in SIBs.">

    <meta property="og:url" content="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y">
    <meta property="og:type" content="article">
    <meta property="og:site_name" content="SpringerLink">
    <meta property="og:title" content="Green Synthesis of Zinc Oxide Nanoparticles Using Leaves Extract of Mariposa Christia vespertilionis and its Potential as Anode Materials in Sodium-Ion Batteries (SIBs) - Arabian Journal for Science and Engineering">
    <meta property="og:description" content="Zinc oxide nanoparticles (ZnO-NPs) is one of the promising material as anode in sodium ion batteries (SIBs). However, due to the large mass and radius of Na-ions, designing electrode materials with high cycling efficiency remains a challenge. One of the attributions is from morphology of ZnO-NPs which can be altered during synthesis process. This study employs Mariposa Christia vespertilionis (MCV) leaves extract to produce ZnO-NP using green synthesis route. This method is safe and cost effective alternative to replace the common chemical methods. Phytochemical test of MCV contains phenols, flavonoids and alkaloids. The formation of ZnO-NPs after calcination at 700, 800 and 900 °C was confirmed via X-ray diffraction and Fourier-transforms infrared spectroscopy analysis. Scanning electron microscope images how irregular shape and agglomerated ZnO-NPs. The average particle sizes of ZnO-NPs range from 38 to 65 nm obtained from high-resolution transmission electron microscope. Nitrogen gas adsorption analysis revealed the pore size and pore volume decreased with the increasing calcination temperatures. The ZnO-NPs calcined at 700 °C exhibits the highest initial discharge capacity of 591 mAh g−1 at 0.1 C up to 100 cycles and better rate capability and could be further exploited as anode materials in SIBs.">
    <meta property="og:image" content="https://static-content.springer.com/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs13369-023-08300-y/MediaObjects/13369_2023_8300_Fig1_HTML.png">

    <script type="application/ld+json">{"mainEntity":{"headline":"Green Synthesis of Zinc Oxide Nanoparticles Using Leaves Extract of Mariposa Christia vespertilionis and its Potential as Anode Materials in Sodium-Ion Batteries (SIBs)","description":"Zinc oxide nanoparticles (ZnO-NPs) is one of the promising material as anode in sodium ion batteries (SIBs). However, due to the large mass and radius of Na-ions, designing electrode materials with high cycling efficiency remains a challenge. One of the attributions is from morphology of ZnO-NPs which can be altered during synthesis process. This study employs Mariposa Christia vespertilionis (MCV) leaves extract to produce ZnO-NP using green synthesis route. This method is safe and cost effective alternative to replace the common chemical methods. Phytochemical test of MCV contains phenols, flavonoids and alkaloids. The formation of ZnO-NPs after calcination at 700, 800 and 900 °C was confirmed via X-ray diffraction and Fourier-transforms infrared spectroscopy analysis. Scanning electron microscope images how irregular shape and agglomerated ZnO-NPs. The average particle sizes of ZnO-NPs range from 38 to 65 nm obtained from high-resolution transmission electron microscope. Nitrogen gas adsorption analysis revealed the pore size and pore volume decreased with the increasing calcination temperatures. The ZnO-NPs calcined at 700 °C exhibits the highest initial discharge capacity of 591 mAh g−1 at 0.1 C up to 100 cycles and better rate capability and could be further exploited as anode materials in SIBs.","datePublished":"2023-10-10T00:00:00Z","dateModified":"2023-10-10T00:00:00Z","pageStart":"623","pageEnd":"635","sameAs":"https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y","keywords":["Zinc oxide","\n     function refreshCartState(json) {

        if (indicator && json.itemCount) {
            indicator.style.display = 'block';

            var moreThanOneItem = json.itemCount > 1;
            indicator.setAttribute('title', "there ".concat(moreThanOneItem ? "are" : "is", " ").concat(json.itemCount, " item").concat(moreThanOneItem ? "s" : "", " in your cart"));
        }
        return json;
    }

                <div data-article-body="true" data-track-component="article body" class="c-article-body">
                    
                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Zinc oxide nanoparticles (ZnO-NPs) is one of the promising material as anode in sodium ion batteries (SIBs). However, due to the large mass and radius of Na-ions, designing electrode materials with high cycling efficiency remains a challenge. One of the attributions is from morphology of ZnO-NPs which can be altered during synthesis process. This study employs <i>Mariposa Christia vespertilionis</i> (MCV) leaves extract to produce ZnO-NP using green synthesis route. This method is safe and cost effective alternative to replace the common chemical methods. Phytochemical test of MCV contains phenols, flavonoids and alkaloids. The formation of ZnO-NPs after calcination at 700, 800 and 900&nbsp;°C was confirmed via X-ray diffraction and Fourier-transforms infrared spectroscopy analysis. Scanning electron microscope images how irregular shape and agglomerated ZnO-NPs. The average particle sizes of ZnO-NPs range from 38 to 65&nbsp;nm obtained from high-resolution transmission electron microscope. Nitrogen gas adsorption analysis revealed the pore size and pore volume decreased with the increasing calcination temperatures. The ZnO-NPs calcined at 700&nbsp;°C exhibits the highest initial discharge capacity of 591 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 C up to 100 cycles and better rate capability and could be further exploited as anode materials in SIBs.</p></div></div></section>

                <div class="c-article-recommendations-list">

                                <div class="main-content">
                                    <section data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">1 </span>Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Nowadays, metal and metal oxide nanoparticles stand out among many energy storage nanomaterials due to their availability, superior conductivity and stability and being environmentally friendly [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ali, R.; Shanan, Z.J.; Saleh, G.M.; Abass, Q.: Green Synthesis and the study of some physical properties of MgO nanoparticles and their antibacterial activity. Iraq. J. Sci. 1, 266–276 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.24996/ijs.2020.61.2.9
                  
                " href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e553">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ifeanyichukwu, U.L.; Fayemi, O.E.; Ateba, C.N.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles from Pomegranate (Punica granatum) extracts and characterization of their antibacterial activity. Molecules (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.3390/molecules25194521
                  
                " href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e553_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lakkaboyana, S.K.; Khantong, S.; Asmel, N.K.; Obaidullah, S.; Kumar, V.; Kannan, K.; Venkateswarlu, K.; Yuzir, A.; Wan Yaacob, W.Z.: Indonesian Kaolin supported nZVI (IK-nZVI) used for the an efficient removal of Pb(II) from aqueous solutions: Kinetics, thermodynamics and mechanism. Environ. Chem. Eng. 9, 106483 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jece.2021.106483
                  
                " href="#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e553_2">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Reddy, N.S.; Vijitha, R.; Naidu, B.R.; Rao, K.K.; Chang-Sik, H.; Venkateswarlu, K.: Benchmarking recent advances in hydrogen production using g-C3N4-based photocatalysts. Nano Energy 31, 108402 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2023.108402
                  
                " href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e553_3">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Akkaya, M.: Usage of graphene-doped tin oxide hybrid nanocomposites in compressor and electromagnetic modeling for single-phase compressor motor. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. 48, 3097–3110 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-022-07116-6
                  
                " href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e553_4">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bandeira, M.; Giovanela, M.; Roesch-Ely, M.; Devine, D.M.; da Silva Crespo, J.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles: A review of the synthesis methodology and mechanism of formation. Sustai. Chem. Pharm. 15, 100223 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scp.2020.100223
                  
                " href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e553_5">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Dharmalingam, P.; Palani, G.; Apsari, R.; Kannan, K.; Lakkaboyana, S.K.; Venkateswarlu, K.; Kumar, V.; Ali, Y.: Synthesis of metal oxides/sulfides-based nanocomposites and their environmental applications: A review. Mater. Today Sustain. 20, 100232 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mtsust.2022.100232
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e556">7</a>]. ZnO-NPs, one of the most appealing metal oxide nanoparticles, possess adjustable size and shape for specific applications. They showcase wide application such as in antibacterial, antifungal, UV-filtering, catalytic, and photochemical traits, alongside high binding energy, wide band gap, and strong piezoelectric properties [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Vaseem, M.; Umar, A.; Hahn, Y.-B.: ZnO nanoparticles: growth, properties, and applications. Metal Oxide Nanostruct. Appl. 5, 10–20 (2010)" href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e559">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Abdelghany, T.M.; Al-Rajhi, A.M.; Yahya, R.; Bakri, M.M.; Al Abboud, M.A.; Yahya, R.; Qanash, H.; Bazaid, A.S.; Salem, S.S.: Phytofabrication of zinc oxide nanoparticles with advanced characterization and its antioxidant, anticancer, and antimicrobial activity against pathogenic microorganisms. Biomass Conv. Biorefinery 13(1), 417–430 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13399-022-03412-1
                  
                " href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e559_1">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Reddy, N.S.; Vijitha, R.; Naidu, B.R.; Rao, K.K.; Chang-Sik, H.; Venkateswarlu, K.: Benchmarking recent advances in hydrogen production using g-C3N4-based photocatalysts. Nano Energy 111, 108402 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2023.108402
                  
                " href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e559_2">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Diachenko, O.; Opanasuyk, A.; Kurbatov, D.; Opanasuyk, N.; Kononov, O.; Nam, D.; Cheong, H.: Surface morphology, structural and optical properties of MgO films obtained by spray pyrolysis technique. Acta. Phys. Pol. 130(3), 805–810 (2016)" href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e559_3">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Ganasan, E.; Yusoff, H.M.; Azmi, A.A.; Chia, P.W.; Lam, S.S.; Kan, S.-Y.; Liew, R.K.; Venkateswarlu, K.; Teo, C.K.: Food additives for the synthesis of metal nanoparticles: A review. Environ. Chem. Lett. 21, 525–538 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10311-022-01473-2
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e562">12</a>]. Batteries are regarded as a critical approach for increasing energy efficiency. Perfect battery electrodes should be inexpensive, harmless, have high energy and power densities for strong capacity and rate performance, last long, and have 100% Coulombic efficiency and stability of electrochemical performance vs cycling. The metal oxide’s high capacities, low cost, simplicity of production and low toxicity make them appealing candidates for ion batteries [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Koo, B.; Xiong, H.; Slater, M.D.; Prakapenka, V.B.; Balasubramanian, M.; Podsiadlo, P.; Johnson, C.S.; Rajh, T.; Shevchenko, E.V.: Hollow iron oxide nanoparticles for application in lithium ion batteries. Nano Lett. 12, 2429–2435 (2012). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/nl3004286
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e565">13</a>].</p><p>ZnO-NPs have been reported to be used in the application of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Gu, L.; Zhang, M.; He, J.; Ni, P.: A porous cross-linked gel polymer electrolyte separator for lithium-ion batteries prepared by using zinc oxide nanoparticle as a foaming agent and filler. Electrochim. Acta 292, 769–778 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.electacta.2018.09.147
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e571">14</a>]. LIBs are a significant power source equivalent to the fossil fuels used in vehicle propulsion and a great energy source for powering electrical vehicles, which are more favourable for the environment. The development of LIBs can improve the variability of renewable energy in the form of highly efficient energy storage devices. However, the resources for LIBs are minimal nowadays, forcing scientists to shift their attention to alternative sources [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Sawicki, M.; Shaw, L.L.: Advances and challenges of sodium ion batteries as post lithium ion batteries. RSC Adv. 5, 53129–53154 (2015). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/c5ra08321d
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e574">15</a>]. To maximise the potential of batteries in terms of safety and energy density [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Bresser, D.; Mueller, F.; Fiedler, M.; Krueger, S.; Kloepsch, R.; Baither, D.; Winter, M.; Paillard, E.; Passerini, S.: Transition-metal-doped zinc oxide nanoparticles as a new lithium-ion anode material. Chem. Mater. 25, 4977–4985 (2013). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/cm403443t
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e577">16</a>] and making sure of the sustainability of these batteries [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Mou, H.; Xiao, W.; Miao, C.; Li, R.; Yu, L.: Tin and tin compound materials as anodes in lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries: A review. Front. Chem. 8, 141 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.3389/fchem.2020.00141
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e580">17</a>], the new electrode materials need to be explored other than optimising the existing batteries [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Bresser, D.; Mueller, F.; Fiedler, M.; Krueger, S.; Kloepsch, R.; Baither, D.; Winter, M.; Paillard, E.; Passerini, S.: Transition-metal-doped zinc oxide nanoparticles as a new lithium-ion anode material. Chem. Mater. 25, 4977–4985 (2013). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/cm403443t
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e583">16</a>]. Hence, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are favoured these days. Sodium-based electrode materials have a similar structure to lithium-based ones, proving their potential to be as good as lithium. SIBs have many advantages as their processing capabilities are more outstanding. The green synthesis method for SIBs anodes is without hydrothermal treatment or unnecessary energy and is practically pollution-free [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yap, Y.H.; Azmi, A.A.; Mohd, N.K.; Yong, F.S.J.; Kan, S.-Y.; Thirmizir, M.Z.A.; Chia, P.W.: Green synthesis of silver nanoparticle using water extract of onion peel and application in the acetylation reaction. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. 45, 4797–4807 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-020-04595-3
                  
                " href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e587">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Naidu, B.R.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Venkateswarlu, K.; Lakkaboyana, S.K.: Highly economic and waste valorization strategy for multicomponent and Knoevenagel reactions using water extract of tamarind seed ash. Environ. Sci. Pollut. Res. 30, 71420–71429 (2023)" href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e587_1">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Appa, R.M.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Naidu, B.R.; Venkateswarlu, K.: Pd-catalyzed oxidative homocoupling of arylboronic acids in WEPA: A sustainable access to symmetrical biaryls under added base and ligand-free ambient conditions. Mol. Catal. 501, 111366 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mcat.2020.111366
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e590">20</a>]. SIBs are also favoured due to their being economically sustainable as the raw material is cheaper than the LIBs as there are abundant of them [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Tarascon, J.-M.: Na-ion versus Li-ion batteries: Complementarity rather than competitiveness. Joule 4, 1616–1620 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.joule.2020.06.003
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e593">21</a>]. The approach involving alloying-based reactions of ZnO-NPs anodes in LIBs is well accepted. In a recent study, the green synthesised ZnO-NPs have shown positive cyclic performance. A recent study has also reported that ZnO-NPs have a lot of potential as anodes in SIBs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Sinha, S.; Didwal, P.N.; Nandi, D.K.; Cho, J.Y.; Kim, S.-H.; Park, C.-J.; Heo, J.: Atomic layer deposited-ZnO@3D-Ni-foam composite for Na-ion battery anode: A novel route for easy and efficient electrode preparation. Ceram. Int. 45, 1084–1092 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ceramint.2018.09.289
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e596">22</a>]. As researchers aim towards a sustainable approach to producing SIBs, the synthesis of ZnO-NPs is done through green synthesis, which is cost-effective and non-toxic to the environment [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Naidu, B.R.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Venkateswarlu, K.; Lakkaboyana, S.K.: Highly economic and waste valorization strategy for multicomponent and Knoevenagel reactions using water extract of tamarind seed ash. Environ. Sci. Pollut. Res. 30, 71420–71429 (2023)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e599">19</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Appa, R.M.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Naidu, B.R.; Venkateswarlu, K.: Pd-catalyzed oxidative homocoupling of arylboronic acids in WEPA: A sustainable access to symmetrical biaryls under added base and ligand-free ambient conditions. Mol. Catal. 501, 111366 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mcat.2020.111366
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e602">20</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Saravanan, M.; Gopinath, V.; Chaurasia, M.K.; Syed, A.; Ameen, F.; Purushothaman, N.: Green synthesis of anisotropic zinc oxide nanoparticles with antibacterial and cytofriendly properties. Microb. Pathog. 115, 57–63 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.micpath.2017.12.039
                  
                " href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e606">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Appa, R.M.; Prasad, S.S.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Naidu, B.R.; Narasimhulu, M.; Venkateswarlu, K.: Palladium-catalysed room-temperature Suzuki-Miyaura coupling in water extract of pomegranate ash, a bio-derived sustainable and renewable medium. Appl. Organomet. Chem. 33, e5126 (2019)" href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e606_1">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Naidu, B.R.; Venkateswarlu, K.: WEPA: a reusable waste biomass-derived catalyst for external oxidant/metal-free quinoxaline synthesis via tandem condensation–cyclization–oxidation of α-hydroxy ketones. Green Chem. 24, 6215–6223 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/D2GC02386E
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e609">25</a>]. The ZnO-NPs synthesised through green synthesis have been proven to give a promising cyclic performance in SIBs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Yusoff, H.M.; Idris, N.H.; Hipul, N.F.; Yusoff, M.; Izham, Z.M.; Bhat, I.U.H.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using black tea extract and its potential as anode material in sodium-ion batteries. Malays. J. Chem. 22(2), 43–51 (2020)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e612">26</a>]. Other common metal oxides such as MgO and Fe<sub>2</sub>O also utilized the green synthesis approach and obtained comparative result with chemical synthesis [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Suppiah, D.D.; Julkapli, N.M.; Sagadevan, S.; Johan, M.R.: Eco-friendly green synthesis approach and evaluation of environmental and biological applications of iron oxide nanoparticles. Inorg. Chem. Commun. 152, 110700 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.inoche.2023.110700
                  
                " href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e617">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mbatha, L.S.; Akinyelu, J.; Chukwuma, C.I.; Mokoena, M.P.; Kudanga, T.: Current trends and prospects for application of green synthesized metal nanoparticles in cancer and COVID-19 therapies. Viruses 15, 741 (2023)" href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e617_1">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hosseinzadeh, E.; Foroumadi, A.; Firoozpour, L.: What is the role of phytochemical compounds as capping agents for the inhibition of aggregation in the green synthesis of metal oxide nanoparticles? A DFT molecular level response. Inorg. Chem. Commun. 147, 110243 (2023)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e620">29</a>]. Hence, further exploration needs to be carried out towards ZnO-NPs via green synthesis to see its potential.</p><p>Over the years, ZnO-NPs using green synthesis method has been carried out using black tea extract [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Yusoff, H.M.; Idris, N.H.; Fatin Hipul, N.; Fazila, N.; Yusoff, M.; Zafirah, N.; Izham, M.; Ul, I.; Bhat, H.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using black tea extract and its potential as anode material in sodium-ion batteries. Malays. J. Chem. 22(20), 43–51 (2020)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e626">30</a>], leaves extract of Stevia [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Agarwal, H.; Shanmugam, V.: A review on anti-inflammatory activity of green synthesized zinc oxide nanoparticle: Mechanism-based approach. Bioorg. Chem. 94, 103423 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.bioorg.2019.103423
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e629">31</a>], leaves extract of <i>Laurus nobilis L</i>. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Fakhari, S.; Jamzad, M.; Kabiri Fard, H.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles: A comparison. Green Chem. 12, 19–24 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1080/17518253.2018.1547925
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e635">32</a>], <i>Aloe barbadensis Mill</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Singh, J.; Kumar, S.; Alok, A.; Upadhyay, S.K.; Rawat, M.; Tsang, D.C.W.; Bolan, N.; Kim, K.-H.: The potential of green synthesized zinc oxide nanoparticles as nutrient source for plant growth. J. Clean. Prod. 214, 1061–1070 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jclepro.2019.01.018
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e642">33</a>], leaves extract of <i>Atalantia monophylla</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Vijayakumar, S.; Mahadevan, S.; Arulmozhi, P.; Sriram, S.; Praseetha, P.K.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using Atalantia monophylla leaf extracts: Characterization and antimicrobial analysis. Mater. Sci. Semicond 82, 39–45 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mssp.2018.03.017
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e648">34</a>], plant extract of <i>Deverra tortuosa</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Selim, Y.A.; Azb, M.A.; Ragab, I.; M HMAE,: A green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using aqueous extract of deverra tortuosa and their cytotoxic activities. Sci. Rep. 10, 3445 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-020-60541-1
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e654">35</a>]. Among the various plant parts such as leaves, bark, seed, root and stem, leaves are particularly distinguished for containing the highest number of active compounds compared to other plant parts [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Momin, K.; Thomas, S.: GC-MS analysis of antioxidant compounds present in different extracts of an endemic plant Dillenia scabrella (dilleniaceae) leaves and barks. Int. J. Pharm. Sci. Res. 11, 2262–2273 (2020)" href="#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e657">36</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lezoul, N.E.H.; Belkadi, M.; Habibi, F.; Guillén, F.: Extraction processes with several solvents on total bioactive compounds in different organs of three medicinal plants. Molecule 25, 4672 (2020)" href="#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e657_1">37</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Petridis, A.; Therios, I.; Samouris, G.; Tananaki, C.: Salinity-induced changes in phenolic compounds in leaves and roots of four olive cultivars (Olea europaea L) and their relationship to antioxidant activity. Environ. Experiment. Botany 79, 37–43 (2012)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e661">38</a>].</p><p>Mariposa C<i>hristia vespertilionis</i> (MCV) is an herbaceous shrub native to Southeast Asia and Brazil that can be found in Malaysia, where it is called ‘Rerama’ by locals [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Osman, M.S.; Ghani, Z.A.; Ismail, N.F.; Razak, N.A.A.; Jaapar, J.; Ariff, M.A.M.: Qualitative comparison of active compounds between red and green Mariposa Christia Vespertillonis leaves extracts. AIP Conf. Proc. 1885, 020282 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1063/1.5002476
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e670">39</a>]. This research aims to develop ZnO-NPs using MCV leaves extract and applied as anode material in SIBs to investigate cyclic performance. The selection of MCV leaves extract is due to its abundant bioactive compounds like polyphenols, alkaloids, and terpenoids with antioxidant and anti-cancer properties [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Osman, M.S.; Ghani, Z.A.; Ismail, N.F.; Razak, N.A.A.; Jaapar, J.; Ariff, M.A.M.: Qualitative comparison of active compounds between red and green Mariposa Christia Vespertillonis leaves extracts. In: AIP Conference Proceedings, American Institute of Physics Inc., 2017." href="#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e673">40</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Farizan, A.F.; Yusoff, H.M.; Badar, N.; Bhat, I.U.H.; Anwar, S.J.; Wai, C.P.; Asari, A.; Kasim, M.F.; Elong, K.: Green synthesis of magnesium oxide nanoparticles using Mariposa christia vespertilionis leaves extract and its antimicrobial study toward S aureus and E coli. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-022-07282-7
                  
                " href="#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e673_1">41</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Nurul, S.A.S.; Hazilawati, H.; Mohd, R.S.; Mohd, F.H.R.; Noordin, M.M.; Norhaizan, M.E.: Subacute oral toxicity assesment of ethanol extract of Mariposa christia vespertilionis leaves in male Sprague Dawley rats. Toxicol. Res. 34, 85–95 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.5487/TR.2018.34.2.085
                  
                " href="#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e673_2">42</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Lee, J.J.; Saiful Yazan, L.; Kassim, N.K.; Che Abdullah, C.A.; Esa, N.; Lim, P.C.; Tan, D.C.: Cytotoxic activity of Christia vespertilionis root and leaf extracts and fractions against breast cancer cell lines. Molecules (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.3390/molecules25112610
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e676">43</a>]. Furthermore, plants containing the most active compounds are more efficient as reducing agents or capping agents [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Yap, Y.H.; Azmi, A.A.; Mohd, N.K.; Yong, F.S.J.; Kan, S.-Y.; Thirmizir, M.Z.A.; Chia, P.W.: Green synthesis of silver nanoparticle using water extract of onion peel and application in the acetylation reaction. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. 45, 4797–4807 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-020-04595-3
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e679">18</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Naidu, B.R.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Venkateswarlu, K.; Lakkaboyana, S.K.: Highly economic and waste valorization strategy for multicomponent and Knoevenagel reactions using water extract of tamarind seed ash. Environ. Sci. Pollut. Res. 30, 71420–71429 (2023)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e683">19</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Iftikhar, M.; Zahoor, M.; Naz, S.; Nazir, N.; Batiha, G.E.-S.; Ullah, R.; Bari, A.; Hanif, M.; Mahmood, H.M.: Green synthesis of silver nanoparticles using Grewia optiva leaf aqueous extract and isolated compounds as reducing agent and their biological activities. J. Nanomater. 2020, 1–10 (2020)" href="#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e686">44</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ezhilarasi, P.; Karthik, P.; Chhanwal, N.; Anandharamakrishnan, C.: Nanoencapsulation techniques for food bioactive components: a review. Food Bioprocess Technol. 6, 628–647 (2013)" href="#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e686_1">45</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Naidu, B.R.; Lakshmidevi, J.; Naik, B.S.S.; Venkateswarlu, K.: Water extract of pomegranate ash as waste-originated biorenewable catalyst for the novel synthesis of chiral tert-butanesulfinyl aldimines in water. Mol. Catal. 511, 111719 (2021)" href="#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e686_2">46</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Aldeen, T.S.; Ahmed Mohamed, H.E.; Maaza, M.: ZnO nanoparticles prepared via a green synthesis approach: Physical properties, photocatalytic and antibacterial activity. J. Phys. Chem. Solids 160, 110313 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jpcs.2021.110313
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e689">47</a>]. By using this plant, further application could be exploited in other study.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Material and Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2 </span>Material and Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.1 </span>Plant Extract Preparation</h3><p>MCV green leaves were collected from Osja Nursery in Rhu Rendang, Marang. For plant extract preparation, the method from [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Vijayakumar, S.; Mahadevan, S.; Arulmozhi, P.; Sriram, S.; Praseetha, P.K.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using Atalantia monophylla leaf extracts: Characterization and antimicrobial analysis. Mater. Sci. Semicond 82, 39–45 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mssp.2018.03.017
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e704">34</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Bala, N.; Saha, S.; Chakraborty, M.; Maiti, M.; Das, S.; Basu, R.; Nandy, P.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using Hibiscus subdariffa leaf extract: effect of temperature on synthesis, anti-bacterial activity and anti-diabetic activity. RSC Adv. 5, 4993–5003 (2015). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/c4ra12784f
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e707">48</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Mahamad Yusoff, N.F.; Idris, N.H.; Md Din, M.F.; Majid, S.R.; Harun, N.A.; Rahman, M.M.: Electrochemical sodiation/desodiation into Mn3O4 nanoparticles. ACS Omega 5(45), 29158–29167 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsomega.0c03888
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e710">49</a>] was adapted with some modifications. After washing with tap water, the green MCV leaves were rinsed with Milli-Q water from Synergy ®UV and dried in an oven at 100&nbsp;°C for 1&nbsp;h. The leaves were blended into fine powders by using a blender.</p><p>Approximately 10&nbsp;g of dry crushed leaves was added to 100&nbsp;ml of Milli-Q in a water bath and left for 20&nbsp;min at 60&nbsp;°C. The leaves extract was cooled at room temperature and filtered using Whatman filter paper No.1. The filtrate was collected. Triplicates of phytochemical test were done towards MCV leaves extract using the method from [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Saidi, N.S.M.; Bhat, H.M.Y.I.U.H.; Appalasamy, S.; Hassim, A.D.M.; Asari, F.Y.A.; Wahab, N.H.A.: Stability and antibacterial properties of green synthesis silver nanoparticles using Nephelium lappaceum peel extract, Malaysian. J. Anal. Sci. 24: 940-953 (2020)." href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e716">50</a>] to investigate the compound’s presence in the extract. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Fig1">1</a> shows overall process from plant extract preparation and finally the phytochemical test. The obtained extract was directly used for the green synthesis of ZnO-NPs.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig. 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs13369-023-08300-y/MediaObjects/13369_2023_8300_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig1" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs13369-023-08300-y/MediaObjects/13369_2023_8300_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure 1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="167"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>MCV leaves extract preparation</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.2 </span>Synthesis of Zinc Oxide Nanoparticles (ZnO-NPs)</h3><p>The precursor used in this experiment was 99% pure zinc acetate dihydrate (Zn (CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>(H<sub>2</sub>O)<sub>2</sub> from Sigma-Aldrich to produce ZnO-NPs. The method from [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Dulta, K.; Koşarsoy Ağçeli, G.; Chauhan, P.; Jasrotia, R.; Chauhan, P.K.: Ecofriendly synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles by Carica papaya leaf extract and their applications. J. Clust. Sci. 33, 603–617 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10876-020-01962-w
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e755">51</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Ramya, V.; Kalaiselvi, V.; Kannan, S.K.; Shkir, M.; Ghramh, H.A.; Ahmad, Z.; Nithiya, P.; Vidhya, N.: Facile synthesis and characterization of zinc oxide nanoparticles using Psidium guajava leaf extract and their antibacterial applications. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. 47, 909–918 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-021-05717-1
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e759">52</a>] was adapted and modified to synthesize ZnO-NPs. 0.1&nbsp;M Zinc acetate dihydrate was stirred for 10&nbsp;min and added to 25&nbsp;ml of the leaf’s extracts in a magnetic stirrer for 2&nbsp;h at 60&nbsp;°C. The light green colour was detected. Centrifuging at 6000&nbsp;rpm for 20&nbsp;min separated particles. The solution was then rinsed with methanol. The precursor powder was obtained after 12&nbsp;h of oven drying at 100&nbsp;°C as can be seen in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Fig2">2</a> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Vijayakumar, S.; Mahadevan, S.; Arulmozhi, P.; Sriram, S.; Praseetha, P.K.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using Atalantia monophylla leaf extracts: Characterization and antimicrobial analysis. Mater. Sci. Semicond 82, 39–45 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mssp.2018.03.017
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e765">34</a>]. ZnO precursor was calcined at 700&nbsp;°C, 800&nbsp;°C and 900&nbsp;°C for 8&nbsp;h [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Yusoff, H.M.; Idris, N.H.; Hipul, N.F.; Yusoff, M.; Izham, Z.M.; Bhat, I.U.H.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using black tea extract and its potential as anode material in sodium-ion batteries. Malays. J. Chem. 22(2), 43–51 (2020)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e768">26</a>].</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Fig. 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs13369-023-08300-y/MediaObjects/13369_2023_8300_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig2" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs13369-023-08300-y/MediaObjects/13369_2023_8300_Fig2_HTML.png" alt="figure 2" loading="lazy" width="685" height="301"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p>The synthesis of ZnO-NPs</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.3 </span>Characterization</h3><p>Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) from PerkinElmer was used to investigate the optimum heat treatment temperature under an atmosphere of nitrogen at a heating rate of 10&nbsp;°C/min; the initial and final temperature was 30 to 900&nbsp;°C, and 0.6&nbsp;g precursor powder was used in TGA. The TGA curves of the metal precursor solution after drying at 100&nbsp;°C to remove the solvent. Fourier transforms infrared (FTIR) (PerkinElmer) was prepared using ATR, and the sample was measured at a resolution of 4000 to 400&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> and 16 scans per sample using 2&nbsp;mg of ZnO-NPs. For morphology studies, samples of ZnO-NPs were observed at with a scanning electron microscope (SEM) (JEOL JSM 6360 LA) and a high-resolution transmission electron microscope (HRTEM) (JEOL JEM-2100 F) with a field emission electron gun (FEG) which is highly bright and stable. For SEM measurements, the particle size of the ZnO-NPs was analysed at two different magnifications, 5,000X and 10,000X, with an acceleration voltage of 15&nbsp;kV and a working distance of 15&nbsp;mm. About half of a small spatula was dissolved in deionized water for the TEM measurement. The sample was put in an ultrasonic bath for 30&nbsp;min to make sure that the crystallites were spread out evenly. The sample of liquid was then put on the TEM grid and heated in an oven for 1&nbsp;h at 80&nbsp;°C. TEM measurements were done with a 200&nbsp;kV accelerating voltage and a field emission electron gun (FEG). X-ray diffraction powder (XRD) was used to analyse&nbsp;the transmission of ZnO-NPs (Shimadzu XRD 600). Bragg-optical Brentano's setup, on the other hand, used CuKα, a scanning speed of 2&nbsp;deg/min, and radiation with the sample spinning from 20 to 80°. A UV–Visible (Shimadzu UV-1800) spectrophotometer measures electromagnetic radiation that includes ultraviolet and visible light and is sent as a wave with a wavelength or frequency between 200 and 800&nbsp;nm pass through quartz cuvette for the absorption spectra of the ZnO-NPs samples using Milli-Q water as a blank reference.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.4 </span>Preparation of Electrode</h3><p>ZnO-NPs nanoparticles, carbon black (Sigma-Aldrich, &gt; 99.5%), and polyvinylidene fluoride (Sigma-Aldrich) were fabricated at a weight ratio of 75:20:5 in Nmethyl-2-pyrrolidone solvent to create working electrodes. A few pieces of labelled copper foil were pasted with homogenous slurry and then, dried at 100&nbsp;°C in a vacuum for 6&nbsp;h. The weight range of active material was measured at around ∼2&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Idris, N.H.; Rahman, M.M.; Wang, J.-Z.; Liu, H.-K.: Microporous gel polymer electrolytes for lithium rechargeable battery application. J. Power. Sources 201, 294–300 (2012). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jpowsour.2011.10.141
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e808">53</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.5 </span>Electrochemical Performance</h3><p>Coin-type cells examined electrode electrochemistry. These cells were performed in an argon-filled glovebox (MBRAUN, Unilab, Germany, H<sub>2</sub>O, O<sub>2</sub> &lt; 0.1&nbsp;ppm) with sodium metal (Sigma-Aldrich, 99.9% trace metal basis) as the counter electrode, a Whatman glass fibre (GF/D) as the separator, and a mixture of 1&nbsp;M NaClO<sub>4</sub> (Sigma-Aldrich, 98%) in propylene carbonate (Sigma-Aldrich, anhydrous, 99.7% pure) with 5 wt% fluoroethylene carbonate (99%) as the electrolyte. A Neware battery analyser conducted galvanostatic cycling between 0.01 and 3.00&nbsp;V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup>. CV was done on a CHI 700E electrochemical workstation at 0.3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> and 0.01–3.00&nbsp;V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Idris, N.H.; Rahman, M.M.; Wang, J.-Z.; Liu, H.-K.: Microporous gel polymer electrolytes for lithium rechargeable battery application. J. Power. Sources 201, 294–300 (2012). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jpowsour.2011.10.141
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e833">53</a>].</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Results and Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec8-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec8"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3 </span>Results and Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec8-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.1 </span>Phytochemical Study</h3><p>Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Tab1">1</a> shows that the MCV extract has alkaloid, flavonoid, saponin, phenolic and tannin. Three times, tests were done and marked A, B, and C to show that the results were always consistent. Only two or more positive results were thought to prove the presence of the investigated compounds in MCV. The flavonoids and alkaloids found in this study are similar to those reported by a previous study which used solvent water [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Awoyinka, O.A.; Balogun, I.O.; Ogunnowo, A.A.: Phytochemical screening and in vitro bioactivity of Cnidoscolus aconitifolius (Euphorbiaceae). J. Med. Plant Res. 1, 63–65 (2007)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e852">54</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Ayandele, A.A.; Adebiyi, A.O.: The phytochemical analysis and antimicrobial screening of extracts of Olax subscorpioidea. Afr. J. Biotechnol. 6, 868–870 (2007)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e855">55</a>]. Furthermore, using water solvent is still comparable to other solvents such as flavonoid and tannin in methanol, hexene, ethyl acetate and acetone solvents [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Dhawan, D.; Gupta, J.: Comparison of different solvents for phytochemical extraction potential from datura metel plant leaves. Int. J. Biol. Chem. 11, 17–22 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.3923/ijbc.2017.17.22
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e858">56</a>].</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 A phytochemical test result of MCV using water extracts</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y/tables/1" aria-label="Full size table 1"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.2 </span>Thermogravimetric Analysis (TGA)</h3><p>Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Fig3">3</a> shows the first weight loss at below 200&nbsp;°C derived from evaporation of the leftover organic solvents. The organic fraction decomposed and was eliminated as CO<sub>2</sub> at these temperatures [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Masud, R.A.; Islam, M.S.; Haque, P.; Khan, M.N.I.; Shahruzzaman, M.; Khan, M.; Takafuji, M.; Rahman, M.M.: Preparation of novel chitosan/poly (ethylene glycol)/ZnO bionanocomposite for wound healing application: Effect of gentamicin loading. Scr. Mater. 12, 100785 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mtla.2020.100785
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1119">57</a>]. At 2 in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Fig3">3</a>, the sudden weight loss of 300–600&nbsp;°C is ascribed to the breakdown of zinc acetate dihydrate and the weight loss constantly decreasing until 580 ºC; afterwards, no significant heat loss can be seen. 700&nbsp;°C, 800&nbsp;°C, and 900&nbsp;°C were chosen as calcination temperatures from this result, and a complete ZnO formation can be known with heating at more than 580&nbsp;°C [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Yusoff, H.M.; Idris, N.H.; Hipul, N.F.; Yusoff, M.; Izham, Z.M.; Bhat, I.U.H.: Green synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles using black tea extract and its potential as anode material in sodium-ion batteries. Malays. J. Chem. 22(2), 43–51 (2020)" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1125">26</a>]. This shows that temperatures from 700 to 900&nbsp;°C are good enough for the thermal decomposition of the metal–organic precursor and fabricated ZnO ion batteries.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Fig. 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><img aria-describedby="Fig3" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs13369-023-08300-y/MediaObjects/13369_2023_8300_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure 3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="585"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>TGA graph of ZnO sample before calcination</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.3 </span>Fourier Transform Infrared Spectroscopy (FTIR)</h3><p>Fourier transform infrared spectroscopy (FTIR) was used to determine the functional groups included into ZNO-NPs production by detecting bond vibrations. Band assignments for all samples analysed during this study are shown in Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Tab2">2</a>. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#Fig4">4</a> shows a comparison of FTIR spectra of calcined ZnO-NPs at three different temperatures (700&nbsp;°C, 800&nbsp;°C, and 900&nbsp;°C). Due to the metal–oxygen stretching mode, peaks at 200&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> to 600&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> resemble metal oxides [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Alswat, A.A.; Bin Ahmad, M.; Saleh, T.A.: Preparation and characterization of zeolite\zinc oxide-copper oxide nanocomposite: Antibacterial activities. Colloid Interface Sci. Commun. 16, 19–24 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.colcom.2016.12.003
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1164">58</a>]. The peak value of 594&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> was obtained in this study used to indicate the stretching modes of the Zn–O bond. As for wavenumber at 895&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> and 964&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> were indicated RCOO<sup>−</sup> or OH<sup>−</sup> group of phenol [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Alamdari, S.; Sasani Ghamsari, M.; Lee, C.; Han, W.; Park, H.H.; Tafreshi, M.J.; Afarideh, H.; Ara, M.H.: Preparation and characterization of zinc oxide nanoparticles using leaf extract of Sambucus ebulus. Appl. Sci. 10(10), 3620 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.3390/app10103620
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1178">59</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Bharathi, D.; Bhuvaneshwari, V.: Synthesis of zinc oxide nanoparticles (ZnO NPs) using pure bioflavonoid rutin and their biomedical applications: antibacterial, antioxidant and cytotoxic activities. Res. Chem. Intermed. 45, 2065–2078 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11164-018-03717-9
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1182">60</a>], significant amounts of phenolic compounds, flavonoids, and amines can be found in plants, and these compounds can be used in the stabilisation, capping and synthesis of nanoparticles [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Chinnathambi, A.; Alharbi, S.A.; Lavarti, R.; Jhanani, G.K.; On-Uma, R.; Jutamas, K.; Anupong, W.: Larvicidal and pupicidal activity of phyto-synthesized zinc oxide nanoparticles against dengue vector aedes aegypti. Environ. Res. 1(216), 114574 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.envres.2022.114574
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1185">61</a>]. According to [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Farizan, A.F.; Yusoff, H.M.; Badar, N.; Bhat, I.U.H.; Anwar, S.J.; Wai, C.P.; Asari, A.; Kasim, M.F.; Elong, K.: Green synthesis of magnesium oxide nanoparticles using Mariposa christia vespertilionis leaves extract and its antimicrobial study toward S aureus and E coli. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-022-07282-7
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1188">41</a>], the stretching vibration of the O–H group is represented by strong absorbance peak at 3000&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> to 4000&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>. The large absorption band about 3742&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> is owing to the presence of several O–H groups on the surface of NPs, which are likely to be common [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Farizan, A.F.; Yusoff, H.M.; Badar, N.; Bhat, I.U.H.; Anwar, S.J.; Wai, C.P.; Asari, A.; Kasim, M.F.; Elong, K.: Green synthesis of magnesium oxide nanoparticles using Mariposa christia vespertilionis leaves extract and its antimicrobial study toward S aureus and E coli. Arab. J. Sci. Eng. (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s13369-022-07282-7
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s13369-023-08300-y#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d87991586e1198">41</a>]. When the annealing temperature was increased, only a broad band of zinc oxide and RCOO– was observed.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table 2 Assignment of FTIR Spectra in MCV</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right
